<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="1434" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png/220px-Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png/330px-Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png/440px-Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/SeaWiFS" title="SeaWiFS">SeaWiFS</a> image for the global biosphere</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Food_consumption.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Food_consumption.gif/220px-Food_consumption.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Food_consumption.gif/330px-Food_consumption.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Food_consumption.gif/440px-Food_consumption.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Food_consumption.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Global average daily <a href="/wiki/Calorie" title="Calorie">calorie</a> consumption in 1995</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2005food_import.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/2005food_import.png/220px-2005food_import.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/2005food_import.png/330px-2005food_import.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/2005food_import.png/440px-2005food_import.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2005food_import.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Food imports in 2005</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Population_density_countries_2017_world_map,_people_per_sq_km.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="864" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg/220px-Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg/330px-Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg/440px-Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Population_density_countries_2017_world_map,_people_per_sq_km.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">Population density</a> by country</div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Food_system" title="Food system">Food systems</a> have complex economic and social <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_value_chain" title="Food value chain">value chains</a> that effect many parts of the global economy.
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">Food industry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_food" title="Genetically modified food">Genetically modified food</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ueberladewagen_(jha).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="710" data-file-width="1094" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/220px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/330px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/440px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ueberladewagen_(jha).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractor</a> pulling a <a href="/wiki/Chaser_bin" title="Chaser bin">chaser bin</a></div></div></div>
<p>Most food has always been obtained through agriculture. With increasing concern over both the methods and products of modern <a href="/wiki/Industrial_agriculture" title="Industrial agriculture">industrial agriculture</a>, there has been a growing trend toward <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_agriculture" title="Sustainable agriculture">sustainable agricultural</a> practices. This approach, partly fueled by consumer demand, encourages <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, local self-reliance and <a href="/wiki/Organic_farming" title="Organic farming">organic farming</a> methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Major influences on food production include international organizations (e.g. the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a>), national government policy (or law), and war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Messer_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Messer-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several organisations have begun calling for a new kind of agriculture in which <a href="/wiki/Agroecosystem" title="Agroecosystem">agroecosystems</a> provide food but also support vital <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a> services so that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertility_(soil)" title="Fertility (soil)">soil fertility</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> are maintained rather than compromised. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Water_Management_Institute" title="International Water Management Institute">International Water Management Institute</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNEP" title="UNEP">UNEP</a>, well-managed agroecosystems not only provide food, fiber and animal products, they also provide services such as <a href="/wiki/Flood_mitigation" title="Flood mitigation">flood mitigation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Groundwater_recharge" title="Groundwater recharge">groundwater recharge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erosion_control" title="Erosion control">erosion control</a> and habitats for plants, birds, fish and other animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_manufacturing">Food manufacturing</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_manufacture" title="Food manufacture">Food manufacture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Food_packages_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1524" data-file-width="2136" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Food_packages_%281%29.jpg/220px-Food_packages_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Food_packages_%281%29.jpg/330px-Food_packages_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Food_packages_%281%29.jpg/440px-Food_packages_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Food_packages_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Packaged household food items</div></div></div>
<p>Packaged foods are manufactured outside the home for purchase. This can be as simple as a <a href="/wiki/Butcher" title="Butcher">butcher</a> preparing meat, or as complex as a modern international <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food industry</a>. Early food processing techniques were limited by available food preservation, packaging, and transportation. This mainly involved <a href="/wiki/Salting_(food)" title="Salting (food)">salting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curing_(food_preservation)" title="Curing (food preservation)">curing</a>, curdling, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drying_(food)" title="Drying (food)">drying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pickling" title="Pickling">pickling</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermentation_(food)" title="Fermentation (food)">fermenting</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smoking_(food)" title="Smoking (food)">smoking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Food manufacturing arose during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a> in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> This development took advantage of new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass-marketing" title="Mass-marketing">mass markets</a> and emerging technology, such as <a href="/wiki/Mill_(grinding)" title="Mill (grinding)">milling</a>, preservation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Packaging" title="Packaging">packaging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Packaging_and_labeling" title="Packaging and labeling">labeling</a>, and transportation. It brought the advantages of pre-prepared time-saving food to the bulk of ordinary people who did not employ domestic servants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jango_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jango-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the start of the 21st century, a two-tier structure has arisen, with a few international food processing giants controlling a wide range of well-known food brands. There also exists a wide array of small local or national food processing companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Advanced technologies have also come to change food manufacture. Computer-based control systems, sophisticated <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">processing</a> and packaging methods, and <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">logistics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_distribution" title="Food distribution">distribution</a> advances can enhance product quality, improve <a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">food safety</a>, and reduce costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jango_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jango-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_food_imports_and_exports">International food imports and exports</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">Population density</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> reported that the European Union was the top food importer in 2005, followed at a distance by the US and Japan. <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>'s need for food was especially well-illustrated in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.  Despite the implementation of <a href="/wiki/Rationing_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rationing in the United Kingdom">food rationing</a>, Britain remained dependent on food imports and the result was a long-term engagement in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a>.
</p><p>Food is traded and marketed on a global basis. The variety and availability of food is no longer restricted by the diversity of locally grown food or the limitations of the local growing season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Between 1961 and 1999, there was a 400% increase in worldwide food exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Some countries are now economically dependent on food exports, which in some cases account for over 80% of all exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, over 100 countries became signatories to the <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_Round" title="Uruguay Round">Uruguay Round</a> of the <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Tariffs_and_Trade" title="General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade">General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade</a> in a dramatic increase in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_liberalization" title="Trade liberalization">trade liberalization</a>. This included an agreement to reduce subsidies paid to farmers, underpinned by the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a> enforcement of <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_policy" title="Agricultural policy">agricultural subsidy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax,_tariff,_and_trade" title="Tax, tariff, and trade">tariffs</a>, import <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quota_Share" title="Quota Share">quotas</a>, and settlement of trade disputes that cannot be bilaterally resolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Where trade barriers are raised on the disputed grounds of public health and safety, the WTO refer the dispute to the <a href="/wiki/Codex_Alimentarius" title="Codex Alimentarius">Codex Alimentarius</a> Commission, which was founded in 1962 by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> and the World Health Organization. Trade liberalization has greatly affected world food trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_and_retailing">Marketing and retailing</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Food_marketing" title="Food marketing">Food marketing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1835" data-file-width="2790" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg/260px-Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg/390px-Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg/520px-Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Packaged food aisles of supermarket in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States of America</a></div></div></div>
<p>Food marketing brings together the producer and the consumer. The marketing of even a single food product can be a complicated process involving many producers and companies. For example, fifty-six companies are involved in making one <a href="/wiki/Canning" title="Canning">can</a> of chicken noodle soup. These businesses include not only chicken and vegetable processors but also the companies that transport the ingredients and those who print labels and manufacture cans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> The food marketing system is the largest direct and indirect non-government employer in the United States.
</p><p>In the pre-modern era, the sale of surplus food took place once a week when farmers took their wares on market day into the local village marketplace. Here food was sold to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grocer" title="Grocer">grocers</a> for sale in their local shops for purchase by local consumers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silhnc_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-silhnc-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jango_108-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jango-108">[108]</a></sup> With the onset of industrialization and the development of the food processing industry, a wider range of food could be sold and distributed in distant locations. Typically early grocery shops would be counter-based shops, in which purchasers told the shop-keeper what they wanted, so that the shop-keeper could get it for them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silhnc_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-silhnc-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Supermarket" title="Supermarket">supermarkets</a> were born. Supermarkets brought with them a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self_service" title="Self service">self service</a> approach to shopping using <a href="/wiki/Shopping_cart" title="Shopping cart">shopping carts</a>, and were able to offer quality food at lower cost through <a href="/wiki/Economies_of_scale" title="Economies of scale">economies of scale</a> and reduced staffing costs. In the latter part of the 20th century, this has been further revolutionized by the development of vast warehouse-sized, out-of-town supermarkets, selling a wide range of food from around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unlike food processors, food retailing is a two-tier market in which a small number of very large <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">companies</a> control a large proportion of supermarkets. The supermarket giants wield great purchasing power over farmers and processors, and strong influence over consumers. Nevertheless, less than 10% of consumer spending on food goes to farmers, with larger percentages going to <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a>, transportation, and intermediate corporations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prices">Prices</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">Food prices</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Food_prices&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">Food prices</a> refer to the average <a href="/wiki/Price_level" title="Price level">price level</a> for food across countries, regions and on a global scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Food prices have an impact on producers and consumers of food.   
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tomatos_Price_Per_Pound.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1060" data-file-width="1413" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Tomatos_Price_Per_Pound.jpg/220px-Tomatos_Price_Per_Pound.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Tomatos_Price_Per_Pound.jpg/330px-Tomatos_Price_Per_Pound.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Tomatos_Price_Per_Pound.jpg/440px-Tomatos_Price_Per_Pound.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tomatos_Price_Per_Pound.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Food pricing for <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a> given in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_dollars" title="US dollars">US dollars</a> per <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pound_(Weight)" title="Pound (Weight)">pound</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FAO_Food_Price_Index_1961%E2%80%932021.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="456" data-file-width="1484" decoding="async" height="68" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/FAO_Food_Price_Index_1961%E2%80%932021.jpg/220px-FAO_Food_Price_Index_1961%E2%80%932021.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/FAO_Food_Price_Index_1961%E2%80%932021.jpg/330px-FAO_Food_Price_Index_1961%E2%80%932021.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/FAO_Food_Price_Index_1961%E2%80%932021.jpg/440px-FAO_Food_Price_Index_1961%E2%80%932021.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FAO_Food_Price_Index_1961%E2%80%932021.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO) Food Price Index 1961â2021 in nominal and real terms. The Real Price Index is the Nominal Price Index deflated by the World Bank Manufactures Unit Value Index (MUV). Years 2014â2016 is 100.</div></div></div>
<p>Price levels depend on the <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food production</a> process, including <a href="/wiki/Food_marketing" title="Food marketing">food marketing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_distribution" title="Food distribution">food distribution</a>. Fluctuation in food prices is determined by a number of compounding factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Geopolitical events, global demand, exchange rates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> government policy, diseases and <a href="/wiki/Crop_yield" title="Crop yield">crop yield</a>, energy costs, availability of natural resources for agriculture,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Food_speculation" title="Food speculation">food speculation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> changes in the use of soil and weather events have a direct impact on the increase or decrease of food prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The consequences of food price fluctuation are multiple. Increases in food prices, or <a href="/wiki/Agflation" title="Agflation">agflation</a>, endangers <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>, particularly for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>, and can cause social unrest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Increases in food prices is related to disparities in diet quality and health,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> particularly among vulnerable populations, such as women and children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>Food prices will <a href="/wiki/Market_trend" title="Market trend">on average continue</a> to rise due to a variety of reasons. Growing <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">world population</a> will put more pressure on the <a href="/wiki/Supply_and_demand" title="Supply and demand">supply and demand</a>. <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate change</a> will increase <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events, including droughts, storms and heavy rain, and overall increases in temperature will have an impact on food production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>To a certain extent, adverse price trends can be counteracted by <a href="/wiki/Food_politics" title="Food politics">food politics</a>.
</p>
An intervention to reduce food loss or waste, if sufficiently large, will affect prices upstream and downstream in the supply chain relative to where the intervention occurred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GrainProducts.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2790" data-file-width="1867" decoding="async" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/GrainProducts.jpg/220px-GrainProducts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/GrainProducts.jpg/330px-GrainProducts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/GrainProducts.jpg/440px-GrainProducts.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GrainProducts.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Some essential food products including <a href="/wiki/Bread" title="Bread">bread</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pasta" title="Pasta">pasta</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_investment">As investment</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Food_speculation" title="Food speculation">Food speculation</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Food_speculation&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Food_speculation" title="Food speculation">Food speculation</a> is betting on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_price" title="Food price">food prices</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unregulated_market" title="Unregulated market">unregulated</a>) <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">financial markets</a>. Food <a href="/wiki/Speculation" title="Speculation">speculation</a> by global players like <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">banks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedge_fund" title="Hedge fund">hedge funds</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pension_fund" title="Pension fund">pension funds</a> is alleged to cause price swings in <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple foods</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soy" title="Soy">soy</a> â even though too large price swings in an idealized economy are theoretically ruled out: <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a> in 1776 reasoned that the only way to make money from commodities trading is by buying low and selling high, which has the effect of smoothing out price swings and mitigating shortages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> For the actors, the apparently random swings are predictable, which means potential huge <a href="/wiki/Profit_(accounting)" title="Profit (accounting)">profits</a>. For the global poor, food speculation and resulting price peaks may result in increased <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a> or even <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>In contrast to food <a href="/wiki/Hoarding_(economics)" title="Hoarding (economics)">hoarding</a>, speculation does not mean that real food shortages or <a href="/wiki/Scarcity" title="Scarcity">scarcity</a> need to be evoked, the price changes are only due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trading" title="Trading">trading</a> activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_speculation_Vidal2011_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_speculation_Vidal2011-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p>
Food speculation may be a reason for <a href="/wiki/Agflation" title="Agflation">agflation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_speculation_NUS_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_speculation_NUS-138">[138]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis" title="2007â08 world food price crisis">2007â08 world food price crisis</a> is thought to have been be partially caused by speculation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_speculation_Vidal2011_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-Food_speculation_Vidal2011-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_speculation_GHOSH_2010_pp._72â86_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_speculation_GHOSH_2010_pp._72â86-140">[140]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Problems">Problems</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USDA_MyPlate_green.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="199" data-file-width="217" decoding="async" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/USDA_MyPlate_green.svg/220px-USDA_MyPlate_green.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/USDA_MyPlate_green.svg/330px-USDA_MyPlate_green.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/USDA_MyPlate_green.svg/440px-USDA_MyPlate_green.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USDA_MyPlate_green.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/MyPlate" title="MyPlate">MyPlate</a> replaced <a href="/wiki/MyPyramid" title="MyPyramid">MyPyramid</a> as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USDA" title="USDA">USDA</a> nutrition guide.</div></div></div>
<p>Because of its centrality to human life, problems related to access, quality and production of food effect every aspect of human life.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nutrition_and_dietary_problems">Nutrition and dietary problems</span></h3>
<p>Between the extremes of optimal health and death from <a href="/wiki/Starvation" title="Starvation">starvation</a> or <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>, there is an array of disease states that can be caused or alleviated by changes in diet. Deficiencies, excesses, and imbalances in diet can produce negative impacts on health, which may lead to various health problems such as <a href="/wiki/Scurvy" title="Scurvy">scurvy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Osteoporosis" title="Osteoporosis">osteoporosis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_2" title="Diabetes mellitus type 2">diabetes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_diseases" title="Cardiovascular diseases">cardiovascular diseases</a> as well as psychological and behavioral problems. The science of nutrition attempts to understand how and why specific dietary aspects influence health.
</p><p>Nutrients in food are grouped into several categories. Macronutrients are fat, protein, and carbohydrates. Micronutrients are the <a href="/wiki/Mineral_(nutrient)" title="Mineral (nutrient)">minerals</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vitamins" title="Vitamins">vitamins</a>. Additionally, food contains water and <a href="/wiki/Dietary_fiber" title="Dietary fiber">dietary fiber</a>.
</p><p>As previously discussed, the body is designed by <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">natural selection</a> to enjoy sweet and fattening foods for evolutionary diets, ideal for <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunters and gatherers</a>. Thus, sweet and fattening foods in nature are typically rare and are very pleasurable to eat. In modern times, with <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">advanced technology</a>, enjoyable foods are easily available to consumers. Unfortunately, this promotes <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a> in adults and children alike.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hunger_and_starvation">Hunger and starvation</span></h3>
<p>Food deprivation leads to malnutrition and ultimately <a href="/wiki/Starvation" title="Starvation">starvation</a>. This is often connected with <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a>, which involves the absence of food in entire communities. This can have a devastating and widespread effect on human health and mortality. <a href="/wiki/Rationing" title="Rationing">Rationing</a> is sometimes used to distribute food in times of shortage, most notably during times of war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Messer_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Messer-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Starvation is a significant international problem. Approximately 815 million people are undernourished, and over 16,000 children die per day from hunger-related causes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Food deprivation is regarded as a deficit need in <a href="/wiki/Maslow%27s_hierarchy_of_needs" title="Maslow's hierarchy of needs">Maslow's hierarchy of needs</a> and is measured using <a href="/wiki/Famine_scales" title="Famine scales">famine scales</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_waste">Food waste</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Food_loss_and_waste" title="Food loss and waste">Food loss and waste</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Food_loss_and_waste&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trashed_vegetables_in_Luxembourg.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Trashed_vegetables_in_Luxembourg.jpeg/220px-Trashed_vegetables_in_Luxembourg.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Trashed_vegetables_in_Luxembourg.jpeg/330px-Trashed_vegetables_in_Luxembourg.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Trashed_vegetables_in_Luxembourg.jpeg/440px-Trashed_vegetables_in_Luxembourg.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trashed_vegetables_in_Luxembourg.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fruit and vegetables in a dumpster, discarded uneaten</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Food_Waste_Fiasco_(15819007150).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1534" data-file-width="2504" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Food_Waste_Fiasco_%2815819007150%29.jpg/220px-Food_Waste_Fiasco_%2815819007150%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Food_Waste_Fiasco_%2815819007150%29.jpg/330px-Food_Waste_Fiasco_%2815819007150%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Food_Waste_Fiasco_%2815819007150%29.jpg/440px-Food_Waste_Fiasco_%2815819007150%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Food_Waste_Fiasco_(15819007150).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Food recovered by food waste critic <a href="/wiki/Rob_Greenfield" title="Rob Greenfield">Rob Greenfield</a> in Madison, Wisconsin, from two days of recovery from dumpsters<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Food_loss_and_waste" title="Food loss and waste">Food loss and waste</a> is food that is not eaten. The causes of food waste or loss are numerous and occur throughout the <a href="/wiki/Food_system" title="Food system">food system</a>, during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_production" title="Food production">production</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">processing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_distribution" title="Food distribution">distribution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grocery_store" title="Grocery store">retail</a> and food service sales, and <a href="/wiki/Social_class_differences_in_food_consumption" title="Social class differences in food consumption">consumption</a>. Overall, about one-third of the world's food is thrown away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> A 2021 <a href="/wiki/Meta-analysis" title="Meta-analysis">metaanalysis</a> that did not include food lost during production, by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> found that food waste was a challenge in all countries at all levels of <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_loss_and_waste_:11_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_loss_and_waste_:11-146">[146]</a></sup> The analysis  estimated that global food waste was 931 million tonnes of food waste (about 121Â kg per capita) across three sectors: 61 per cent from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Household_waste" title="Household waste">households</a>, 26 per cent from <a href="/wiki/Foodservice" title="Foodservice">food service</a> and 13 per cent from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_retailer" title="Food retailer">retail</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_loss_and_waste_:11_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-Food_loss_and_waste_:11-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p><p>Food loss and waste is a major part of the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions_from_agriculture" title="Greenhouse gas emissions from agriculture">impact of agriculture on climate change</a> (it amounts to 3.3 billion tons of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">CO<sub>2</sub>e emissions</a> annually<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_loss_and_waste_:15_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_loss_and_waste_:15-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>) and other <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_agriculture" title="Environmental impact of agriculture">environmental issues</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">land use</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_footprint" title="Water footprint">water use</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">loss of biodiversity</a>. Prevention of food waste is the highest priority, and when prevention is not possible, the food waste hierarchy ranks the food waste treatment options from preferred to least preferred based on their negative environmental impacts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Reuse pathways of surplus food intended for human consumption, such as food donation, is the next best strategy after prevention, followed by <a href="/wiki/Animal_feed" title="Animal feed">animal feed</a>, recycling of nutrients and energy followed by the least preferred option, <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfill</a>, which is a major source of the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> Other considerations include unreclaimed phosphorus in food waste leading to further <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phosphate_mining" title="Phosphate mining">phosphate mining</a>. Moreover, reducing food waste in all parts of the <a href="/wiki/Food_system" title="Food system">food system</a> is an important part of reducing the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_agriculture" title="Environmental impact of agriculture">environmental impact of agriculture</a>, by reducing the total amount of water, <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">land</a>, and other resources used.
</p>
The UN's <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_12" title="Sustainable Development Goal 12">Sustainable Development Goal Target 12.3</a>  seeks to "halve global per capita food waste at the retail and consumer levels and reduce food losses along production and supply chains, including post-harvest losses" by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_loss_and_waste_:17_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_loss_and_waste_:17-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">Climate change mitigation</a> strategies prominently feature reducing food waste.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_loss_and_waste_:4_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_loss_and_waste_:4-152">[152]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy">Policy</span></h2>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Food_policy" title="Food policy">Food policy</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Food_policy&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Food_policy" title="Food policy">Food policy</a> is the area of <a href="/wiki/Public_policy" title="Public policy">public policy</a> concerning how food is produced, processed, distributed, purchased, or provided. Food policies are designed to influence the operation of the food and agriculture system balanced with ensuring human health needs. This often includes decision-making around production and processing techniques, marketing, availability, utilization, and consumption of food, in the interest of meeting or furthering social objectives. Food policy can be promulgated on any level, from local to global, and by a government agency, business, or organization. Food policymakers engage in activities such as regulation of food-related industries, establishing eligibility standards for food assistance programs for the poor, ensuring safety of the food supply, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_labeling" title="Food labeling">food labeling</a>, and even the qualifications of a product to be considered <a href="/wiki/Organic_food" title="Organic food">organic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_policy_What_is_a_food_policy?_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_policy_What_is_a_food_policy?-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Holding_rice.jpg"><img alt="Picture of hands holding rice." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="357" data-file-width="282" decoding="async" height="279" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Holding_rice.jpg/220px-Holding_rice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f3/Holding_rice.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Holding_rice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rice</div></div></div>
<p>Most food policy is initiated at the domestic level for purposes of ensuring a safe and adequate food supply for the citizenry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_policy_Linked_National_Models_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_policy_Linked_National_Models-154">[154]</a></sup> In a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_nation" title="Developing nation">developing nation</a>, there are three main objectives for food policy: to protect the poor from crises, to develop long-run markets that enhance efficient resource use, and to increase food production that will in turn promote an increase in income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_policy_Managing_food_price_risks_and_instability_in_a_liberalizing_market_environment_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_policy_Managing_food_price_risks_and_instability_in_a_liberalizing_market_environment-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>Food policy comprises the mechanisms by which food-related matters are addressed or administered by governments, including international bodies or networks, and by public institutions or private organizations. Agricultural producers often bear the burden of governments' desire to keep <a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">food prices</a> sufficiently low for growing urban populations. Low prices for consumers can be a disincentive for farmers to produce more food, often resulting in hunger, poor trade prospects, and an increased need for food imports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_policy_Linked_National_Models_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-Food_policy_Linked_National_Models-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
In a more developed country such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, food and nutrition policy must be viewed in context with regional and national economic concerns, environmental pressures, maintenance of a <a href="/wiki/Social_safety_net" title="Social safety net">social safety net</a>, health, encouragement of private enterprise and innovation, and an agrarian landscape dominated by fewer, larger mechanized farms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_policy_Wilde_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_policy_Wilde-156">[156]</a></sup> Industrialized countries strive to ensure that farmers earn relatively stable incomes despite price and supply fluctuations and adverse weather events. The cost of subsidizing farm incomes is passed along to consumers in the form of higher food prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_policy_Linked_National_Models_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-Food_policy_Linked_National_Models-154">[154]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_definition">Legal definition</span></h3>
<p>Some countries list a legal definition of food, often referring them with the word <i>foodstuff</i>. These countries list food as any item that is to be processed, partially processed, or unprocessed for consumption. The listing of items included as food includes any substance intended to be, or reasonably expected to be, ingested by humans. In addition to these foodstuffs, drink, <a href="/wiki/Chewing_gum" title="Chewing gum">chewing gum</a>, water, or other items processed into said food items are part of the legal definition of food. Items not included in the legal definition of food include <a href="/wiki/Pet_food" title="Pet food">animal feed</a>, live animals (unless being prepared for sale in a market), plants prior to harvesting, medicinal products, <a href="/wiki/Cosmetics" title="Cosmetics">cosmetics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> and tobacco products, <a href="/wiki/Narcotic" title="Narcotic">narcotic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychotropic_substance" title="Psychotropic substance">psychotropic substances</a>, and residues and contaminants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Right_to_food">Right to food</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Right_to_food" title="Right to food">Right to food</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Right_to_food&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:422px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Right_to_Food_World_Map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="863" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Right_to_Food_World_Map.svg/420px-Right_to_Food_World_Map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Right_to_Food_World_Map.svg/630px-Right_to_Food_World_Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Right_to_Food_World_Map.svg/840px-Right_to_Food_World_Map.svg.png 2x" width="420"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Right_to_Food_World_Map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Right to food around the world (as of 2011-2012).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_Knuth_2011_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_Knuth_2011-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_ReferenceA_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_ReferenceA-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_ReferenceB_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_ReferenceB-160">[160]</a></sup><br/> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#8933bf; color:white;">Â </span>Â Adopted or drafting a framework law (19).</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#2fa5b0; color:black;">Â </span>Â Constitutional, explicit as a right (23).</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#60c840; color:black;">Â </span>Â Constitutional, implicit in broader rights or as directive principle (41).</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#d9bf2d; color:black;">Â </span>Â Direct applicability via international treaties (103).</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#c85f47; color:black;">Â </span>Â Committed by ratifying the <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Economic,_Social_and_Cultural_Rights" title="International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights">International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights</a> (160).</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#e0e0e0; color:black;">Â </span>Â No known right to food.</div> Note: The same country can fall in multiple categories; the colour given to a country corresponds to the highest listed category in which a country falls.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Right_to_food" title="Right to food">right to food</a>, and its variations, is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_right" title="Human right">human right</a> protecting the right of people to feed themselves in <a href="/wiki/Dignity" title="Dignity">dignity</a>, implying that sufficient food is available, that people have the means to access it, and that it adequately meets the individual's <a href="/wiki/Diet_(nutrition)" title="Diet (nutrition)">dietary</a> needs. The right to food protects the right of all human beings to be free from <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">hunger</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_insecurity" title="Food insecurity">food insecurity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_Ziegler_2012_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_Ziegler_2012-161">[161]</a></sup> The right to food does not imply that governments have an obligation to hand out free food to everyone who wants it, or a right to be fed. However, if people are deprived of access to food for reasons beyond their control, for example, because they are in detention, in times of war or after natural disasters, the right requires the government to provide food directly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_ReferenceC_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_ReferenceC-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p><p>The right is derived from the <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Economic,_Social_and_Cultural_Rights" title="International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights">International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_ReferenceC_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_ReferenceC-162">[162]</a></sup> which has 170 state parties as of April 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_ReferenceA_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_ReferenceA-159">[159]</a></sup> States that sign the covenant agree to take steps to the maximum of their available resources to achieve progressively the full realization of the right to adequate food, both nationally and internationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_Ziegler_2012_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_Ziegler_2012-161">[161]</a></sup> In a total of 106 countries the right to food is applicable either via constitutional arrangements of various forms or via direct applicability in law of various international treaties in which the right to food is protected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_harvnb|Knuth|2011_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_harvnb|Knuth|2011-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the 1996 <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Summit" title="World Food Summit">World Food Summit</a>, governments reaffirmed the right to food and committed themselves to halve the number of hungry and malnourished from 840 to 420 million by 2015. However, the number has increased over the past years, reaching an infamous record in 2009 of more than 1 billion undernourished people worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Right_to_food_Ziegler_2012_161-2"><a href="#cite_note-Right_to_food_Ziegler_2012-161">[161]</a></sup> Furthermore, the number who suffer from hidden hunger â micronutrient deficiences that may cause stunted bodily and intellectual growth in children â amounts to over 2 billion people worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>
</p><p>Whilst under international law states are obliged to respect, protect and fulfill the right to food, the practical difficulties in achieving this human right are demonstrated by prevalent food insecurity across the world, and ongoing litigation in countries such as India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> In the continents with the biggest food-related problems â <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> â not only is there shortage of food and lack of infrastructure but also maldistribution and inadequate access to food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
The Human Rights Measurement Initiative<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> measures the right to food for countries around the world, based on their level of income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_security">Food security</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">Food security</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Food_security&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Africa_Food_Security_18_(10665134354).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2825" data-file-width="1880" decoding="async" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Africa_Food_Security_18_%2810665134354%29.jpg/220px-Africa_Food_Security_18_%2810665134354%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Africa_Food_Security_18_%2810665134354%29.jpg/330px-Africa_Food_Security_18_%2810665134354%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Africa_Food_Security_18_%2810665134354%29.jpg/440px-Africa_Food_Security_18_%2810665134354%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Africa_Food_Security_18_(10665134354).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A woman selling <a href="/wiki/Produce" title="Produce">produce</a> at a market in <a href="/wiki/Lilongwe" title="Lilongwe">Lilongwe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Africa_Food_Security_21_(10665132276).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4992" data-file-width="3328" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Africa_Food_Security_21_%2810665132276%29.jpg/220px-Africa_Food_Security_21_%2810665132276%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Africa_Food_Security_21_%2810665132276%29.jpg/330px-Africa_Food_Security_21_%2810665132276%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Africa_Food_Security_21_%2810665132276%29.jpg/440px-Africa_Food_Security_21_%2810665132276%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Africa_Food_Security_21_(10665132276).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A farmer holding up <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Onions" title="Onions">onions</a> he has grown on his farm near <a href="/wiki/Gilgil" title="Gilgil">Gilgil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">Food security</a> is the measure of the availability of food and individuals' <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">ability to access it</a>. According to the United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_World_Food_Security" title="Committee on World Food Security">Committee on World Food Security</a>, food security is defined as meaning that all people, at all times, have physical, social, and economic access to sufficient, safe, and nutritious food that meets their food preferences and dietary needs for an active and healthy life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_:6_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_:6-171">[171]</a></sup> The availability of food irrespective of class, gender or region is another one. There is evidence of food security being a concern many thousands of years ago, with central authorities in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_China" title="Ancient China">ancient China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a> being known to release food from storage in times of famine. At the 1974 <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Conference" title="World Food Conference">World Food Conference</a>, the term "food security" was defined with an emphasis on supply; food security is defined as the "availability at all times of adequate, nourishing, diverse, balanced and moderate world food supplies of basic foodstuffs to sustain a steady expansion of food consumption and to offset fluctuations in production and prices".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Later definitions added demand and access issues to the definition. The first World Food Summit, held in 1996, stated that food security "exists when all people, at all times, have physical and economic access to sufficient, safe and nutritious food to meet their dietary needs and food preferences for an active and healthy life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_FAO_1996_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_FAO_1996-174">[174]</a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Household" title="Household">household</a> food security is considered to exist when all members, at all times, have access to enough food for an active, <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">healthy</a> life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_usda_measuring_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_usda_measuring-175">[175]</a></sup> Individuals who are food secure do not live in <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">hunger</a> or fear of <a href="/wiki/Starvation" title="Starvation">starvation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_FAO_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_FAO-176">[176]</a></sup> Food insecurity, on the other hand, is defined by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">United States Department of Agriculture</a> (USDA) as a situation of "limited or uncertain availability of nutritionally adequate and safe foods or limited or uncertain ability to acquire acceptable foods in socially acceptable ways".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_Bickel_2000_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_Bickel_2000-177">[177]</a></sup> Food security incorporates a measure of resilience to future disruption or unavailability of critical food supply due to various risk factors including droughts, shipping disruptions, fuel shortages, economic instability, and wars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_FAO,_WFP,_IFAD_2013_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_FAO,_WFP,_IFAD_2013-178">[178]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> of the United Nations, or FAO, identified the four pillars of food security as availability, access, utilization, and stability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_autogenerated2009_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_autogenerated2009-179">[179]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN) recognized the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right_to_Food" title="Right to Food">Right to Food</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Declaration of Human Rights</a> in 1948,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_FAO_176-1"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_FAO-176">[176]</a></sup> and has since said that it is vital for the enjoyment of all other rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>
</p>
The 1996 World Summit on Food Security declared that "food should not be used as an instrument for political and economic pressure".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_FAO_1996_174-1"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_FAO_1996-174">[174]</a></sup> Multiple different international agreements and mechanisms have been developed to address food security. The main global policy to reduce hunger and poverty is in the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>. In particular <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_2" title="Sustainable Development Goal 2">Goal 2: Zero Hunger</a> sets globally agreed on targets to end hunger, achieve food security and improved nutrition, and promote <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_agriculture" title="Sustainable agriculture">sustainable agriculture</a> by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_security_:5_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_security_:5-181">[181]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_aid">International aid</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_aid" title="Food aid">Food aid</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_aid" title="Food aid">Food aid</a> can benefit people suffering from a shortage of food. It can be used to improve peoples' lives in the short term, so that a society can increase its standard of living to the point that food aid is no longer required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Conversely, badly managed food aid can create problems by disrupting local markets, depressing crop prices, and discouraging food production. Sometimes a cycle of food aid dependence can develop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Its provision, or threatened withdrawal, is sometimes used as a political tool to influence the policies of the destination country, a strategy known as <a href="/wiki/Food_politics" title="Food politics">food politics</a>. Sometimes, food aid provisions will require certain types of food be purchased from certain sellers, and food aid can be misused to enhance the markets of donor countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> International efforts to distribute food to the neediest countries are often coordinated by the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">Food safety</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SalmonellaNIAID.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1761" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/SalmonellaNIAID.jpg/220px-SalmonellaNIAID.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/SalmonellaNIAID.jpg/330px-SalmonellaNIAID.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/SalmonellaNIAID.jpg/440px-SalmonellaNIAID.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SalmonellaNIAID.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Salmonella" title="Salmonella">Salmonella</a> bacteria is a common cause of foodborne illness, particularly in undercooked <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chicken</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicken_egg" title="Chicken egg">chicken eggs</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Foodborne_illness" title="Foodborne illness">Foodborne illness</a>, commonly called "food poisoning", is caused by <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toxin" title="Toxin">toxins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">parasites</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prion" title="Prion">prions</a>. Roughly 7 million people die of food poisoning each year, with about 10 times as many suffering from a non-fatal version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MedlinePlus_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-MedlinePlus-186">[186]</a></sup> The two most common factors leading to cases of bacterial foodborne illness are cross-contamination of ready-to-eat food from other uncooked foods and improper temperature control. Less commonly, acute adverse reactions can also occur if chemical contamination of food occurs, for example from improper storage, or use of non-food grade soaps and disinfectants. Food can also be adulterated by a very wide range of articles (known as "foreign bodies") during farming, manufacture, cooking, packaging, distribution, or sale. These foreign bodies can include pests or their droppings, hairs, cigarette butts, wood chips, and all manner of other contaminants. It is possible for certain types of food to become contaminated if stored or presented in an unsafe container, such as a ceramic pot with lead-based glaze.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MedlinePlus_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-MedlinePlus-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_poisoning" title="Food poisoning">Food poisoning</a> has been recognized as a disease since as early as Hippocrates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> The sale of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rancidity" title="Rancidity">rancid</a>, contaminated, or adulterated food was commonplace until the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Hygiene" title="Hygiene">hygiene</a>, refrigeration, and vermin controls in the 19th century. Discovery of techniques for killing bacteria using heat, and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbiological" title="Microbiological">microbiological</a> studies by scientists such as <a href="/wiki/Louis_Pasteur" title="Louis Pasteur">Louis Pasteur</a>, contributed to the modern sanitation standards that are ubiquitous in developed nations today. This was further underpinned by the work of <a href="/wiki/Justus_von_Liebig" title="Justus von Liebig">Justus von Liebig</a>, which led to the development of modern <a href="/wiki/Food_storage" title="Food storage">food storage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_preservation" title="Food preservation">food preservation</a> methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> In more recent years, a greater understanding of the causes of food-borne illnesses has led to the development of more systematic approaches such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hazard_Analysis_and_Critical_Control_Points" title="Hazard Analysis and Critical Control Points">Hazard Analysis and Critical Control Points</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HACCP" title="HACCP">HACCP</a>), which can identify and eliminate many risks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup>
</p><p>Recommended measures for ensuring food safety include maintaining a clean preparation area with foods of different types kept separate, ensuring an adequate cooking temperature, and refrigerating foods promptly after cooking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>Foods that spoil easily, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meats" title="Meats">meats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dairy" title="Dairy">dairy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a>, must be prepared a certain way to avoid contaminating the people for whom they are prepared. As such, the rule of thumb is that cold foods (such as dairy products) should be kept cold and hot foods (such as soup) should be kept hot until storage. Cold meats, such as chicken, that are to be cooked should not be placed at room temperature for thawing, at the risk of dangerous bacterial growth, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Salmonella" title="Salmonella">Salmonella</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Escherichia_coli" title="Escherichia coli">E. coli</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allergies">Allergies</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Food_allergy" title="Food allergy">Food allergy</a></div>
<p>Some people have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allergies" title="Allergies">allergies</a> or sensitivities to foods that are not problematic to most people. This occurs when a person's <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a> mistakes a certain food protein for a harmful foreign agent and attacks it. About 2% of adults and 8% of children have a food allergy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allergy_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-allergy-192">[192]</a></sup> The amount of the food substance required to provoke a reaction in a particularly susceptible individual can be quite small. In some instances, traces of food in the air, too minute to be perceived through smell, have been known to provoke lethal reactions in extremely sensitive individuals. Common food allergens are <a href="/wiki/Gluten" title="Gluten">gluten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shellfish" title="Shellfish">shellfish</a> (mollusks), <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanuts</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soy" title="Soy">soy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allergy_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-allergy-192">[192]</a></sup> Allergens frequently produce symptoms such as <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrhea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rash" title="Rash">rashes</a>, bloating, <a href="/wiki/Vomiting" title="Vomiting">vomiting</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Regurgitation_(digestion)" title="Regurgitation (digestion)">regurgitation</a>. The digestive complaints usually develop within half an hour of ingesting the <a href="/wiki/Allergen" title="Allergen">allergen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allergy_192-2"><a href="#cite_note-allergy-192">[192]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rarely, food allergies can lead to a <a href="/wiki/Medical_emergency" title="Medical emergency">medical emergency</a>, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anaphylactic_shock" title="Anaphylactic shock">anaphylactic shock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hypotension" title="Hypotension">hypotension</a> (low blood pressure), and loss of consciousness. An allergen associated with this type of reaction is peanut, although <a href="/wiki/Latex" title="Latex">latex</a> products can induce similar reactions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allergy_192-3"><a href="#cite_note-allergy-192">[192]</a></sup> Initial treatment is with <a href="/wiki/Epinephrine_(medication)" title="Epinephrine (medication)">epinephrine</a> (adrenaline), often carried by known patients in the form of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epi-pen" title="Epi-pen">Epi-pen</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twinject" title="Twinject">Twinject</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_health_issues">Other health issues</span></h3>
<p>Human diet was estimated to cause perhaps around 35% of <a href="/wiki/Diet_and_cancer" title="Diet and cancer">cancers</a> in a human epidemiological analysis by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Doll" title="Richard Doll">Richard Doll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Peto" title="Richard Peto">Richard Peto</a> in 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup>  These cancer may be caused by <a href="/wiki/Carcinogen" title="Carcinogen">carcinogens</a> that are present in food naturally or as contaminants. Food contaminated with fungal growth may contain <a href="/wiki/Mycotoxin" title="Mycotoxin">mycotoxins</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aflatoxins" title="Aflatoxins">aflatoxins</a> which may be found in contaminated corn and peanuts.
